<div id="review_421042778" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/421042778" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/421042778?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25380932-a-hunger-like-no-other">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=not-your-ordinary-creatures">not-your-ordinary-creatures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=rabid-reads-reviews">rabid-reads-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=weres-shapeshifters">weres-shapeshifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=some-kinda-magic">some-kinda-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=jerk-of-my-dreams">jerk-of-my-dreams</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=favorite-secondary-characters">favorite-secondary-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=dead-things">dead-things</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=angels-and-or-demons">angels-and-or-demons</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer421042778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18434978195585199490"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2014/06/review-a-hunger-like-no-other-by-kresley-cole.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/><i>A Hunger Like No Other</i> is actually the first book I read in Kresley Cole's <i>Immortals After Dark</i> (my favorite PNR) series. I went back and read <i>The Warlord Wants Forever</i> when I finished it b/c I wanted to know what was going on with Myst and Wroth (you could tell there was a story there, but had no idea what it was). For that reason, I recommend reading <i>The Warlord Wants Forever</i> first, even though it's a more of a short story than a full installment.<br/><br/>In <i>A Hunger Li</i></span>
  <span id="freeText18434978195585199490" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br><br><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2014/06/review-a-hunger-like-no-other-by-kresley-cole.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br><i>A Hunger Like No Other</i> is actually the first book I read in Kresley Cole's <i>Immortals After Dark</i> (my favorite PNR) series. I went back and read <i>The Warlord Wants Forever</i> when I finished it b/c I wanted to know what was going on with Myst and Wroth (you could tell there was a story there, but had no idea what it was). For that reason, I recommend reading <i>The Warlord Wants Forever</i> first, even though it's a more of a short story than a full installment.<br><br>In <i>A Hunger Like No Other</i>, we meet Emmaline Troy, a Valkyrie/vampire hybrid, and Lachlain MacRieve, King of the Lykae.<br><br>Emma is in Paris looking for information about her father.<br><br>Her Valkyrie mother died of HEARTBREAK shortly after Emma was born, never revealing to anyone who the father of her child was. All anyone knew was that she had been in Paris with him until she returned to her coven in New Orleans with baby Emma in tow.<br><br>SO. Off to Paris Emma goes.<br><br>After spending a semester there taking night classes and researching, Emma has nothing to show for her time abroad except disappointment. She is about to be recalled home to Louisiana where she can be kept safe from some vague threat when she is attacked by a very large, very hot, very ANGRY man.<br><br>Lachlain MacRieve has been held captive and tortured for over 150 years.<br><br>The vampires have made the catacombs under Paris their very own personal prison where they subject their enemies to unbelievable cruelty. For Lachlain that means being chained in front of a roaring fire that waxes and wans, burning him over and over again, but never killing him b/c he is IMMORTAL. He simply burns until he passes out, only to reawaken when his body has adequately healed him only to endure more torture.<br><br>Until her smells <i>her</i>, his <i>mate</i>. The woman he has been looking for for nearly a <i>millennia</i>.<br><br>*rolls eyes*<br><br>I'm wracking my brain trying to come up with a way to make all of this sound less ridiculous, but I can't. Maybe it <i>is</i> ridiculous and I just don't care b/c I love this series.<br><br>Despite that love, I think this is my least favorite IAD book.<br><br>The Emmaline at the beginning of book is <i>vastly</i> different from the kickass Emma at end of the book, but end-of-book Emma can't entirely make up for the spineless ninny that is early Emma.<br><br>And Emma's little epiphany moment is both confusing, and once you figure out where she's going with it, hard to accept. She seems to mark, with pin-point accuracy, the pivotal moment that turned her into a big fraidy-cat, and this "aha" only served to make me have a, "sure . . . whatever you say, boss" moment of my own.<br><br>But, like I already said, by the end, Emma is straight-up kickass. Kicking <i>lycae</i> ass, kickass. And this happens slowly and incrementally enough that it's believable.<br><br>Lachlain, on the other hand, is a RAGE monster pretty much from beginning to end.<br><br>And I know that I said in my <b>
  <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2014/03/review-the-warlord-wants-forever-by-kresley-cole.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <em>The Warlord Wants Forever</em>
  </a>
</b> review that I am totally down with <i>intensely</i> sexually aggressive males, but Lachlain is a little bit OTT, even for me. His early interactions with Emma skate that fine line between aggressively <i>hot</i> and aggressively-bound-for-prison so closely that it's uncomfortable. Especially taking into consideration that early Emma was a spineless ninny. If she wasn't, and she gave as good as she got, then it probably would have worked for me, but as it was . . . Emma's fine line between arousal and terror . . . not a big fan.<br><br>But I do love this series, and once RAGE monster Lachlain starts controlling himself a bit better, and Emma grows a backbone, I remembered why. There is, however, no denying that the early stages of their "courtship" were rough. If you have a problem with that sort of thing, I'd skip this one, but if you're more of a "the end justifies the means"person, you should be fine. The uncomfortable part is fairly brief, and the rest of it is typical Cole awesomeness. Your call. But don't let one scary RAGE monster scare you off the whole series, b/c then you would be missing out.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>My other reviews for this series:</b><br><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/421306605" rel="nofollow noopener">The Warlord Wants Forever (Immortals After Dark #1)</a>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="18434978195585199490" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_389209478" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/389209478" />
    <a title="Kelly H. (Maybedog)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog"><img alt="Kelly H. (Maybedog)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366465767p2/1059653.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/389209478?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly H. (Maybedog)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly H. (Maybedog)" href="/user/show/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog">Kelly H. (Maybedog)</a>
      </span>

          marked it as never


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781849834186" href="/book/show/9674479-a-hunger-like-no-other">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">No one</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=what-not-mm">what-not-mm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=why-due-to-author">why-due-to-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=why-full-of-hate">why-full-of-hate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=what-modern-fantasy">what-modern-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1059653-kelly-h-maybedog?shelf=what-danger-danger-wilma-robinson">what-danger-danger-wilma-robinson</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer389209478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7071224624420880819">Apparently this series is all about the women being bullied into submission by the "hero" of the story. The first one is apparently a little "rapey" in that the sex scene starts off forced and then the woman eventually submits. But in this book the hero actually rapes someone and a popular reviewer/friend says the heroine doesn't have any ill effects or even a problem with it really. The rapey-ness is a common enough theme with were-whatevers and I have a problem enough with that, but out and ou</span>
  <span id="freeText7071224624420880819" style="display:none">Apparently this series is all about the women being bullied into submission by the "hero" of the story. The first one is apparently a little "rapey" in that the sex scene starts off forced and then the woman eventually submits. But in this book the hero actually rapes someone and a popular reviewer/friend says the heroine doesn't have any ill effects or even a problem with it really. The rapey-ness is a common enough theme with were-whatevers and I have a problem enough with that, but out and out rape, by the hero no less, I can't stomach no matter how remorseful he may be later (I don't know if that's even the case, I'm just hoping it is because I have a friend who loved this book.)<br /><br />Another friend who disliked the book described it this way,<br /><br />"He practically rapes her, he threatens her life, he molests her, he forces her to perform sexual acts on him against her will, kidnaps her, steals her credit card and decks himself out like James Bond, trashes every hotel room rented under HER name, then holds her hostage in his castle....but she falls for him within a week! There is hope for sexual predators everywhere. Just growl that you're meant to be together, and every felonies you've committed just fades away. I can't wait for the wedding day film reel...so romantic."<br /> Jenn (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124554943" rel="nofollow noopener">see full review</a>)<br /><br />I'll admit I have a problem with this violent alpha male thing treating women like trash, even when the woman is smart and strong and doesn't let it affect her self-esteem. For example, I love the Mercy Thompson series except I just can't stand her tolerance for how the men treat her. I finally had to stop reading them. But the reviewer mentioned in the first paragraph above actually really likes that series so she isn't nearly as sensitive to this stuff as I am. And she still hated both the first and second (as did several people who agreed with her review.) <br /><br />If you're interested in why I have such a problem with Mercy Thompson, here's an extract from my review of the second: <br /><br />"This is the annoying Heinlein-esque sexism: you know the guy is a jerk and you know better but let's just humor him. The reality is that in by going along with him with his macho bullshit, he still gets all the power and control. Just because you're going along voluntarily doesn't make it equality."<br /><br />This book sounds way, way worse. (Although I hear that later in that series it's really not so very different.)<br /><br />BUT<br /><br />This powerful, on the verge of violence, were-creature thing can be done right. The one example I'm familiar with is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/21748.Ilona_Andrews" title="Ilona Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener">Ilona Andrews</a>'s series beginning with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/38619.Magic_Bites__Kate_Daniels___1_" title="Magic Bites (Kate Daniels, #1) by Ilona Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener">Magic Bites</a> has an alpha were who is strong and scary and wants the heroine. While she thinks he's physically attractive, she refers to him as a psychopath and feels herself lucky when she leaves his presence with no bloodshed. They end pretty much every encounter in a fight because he's controlling. But although all werea are potentially very violent, alphas are both male and female. He of course is King of all of them because this is, after all, fantasy fiction. But the main character refuses to submit to his ways and makes him adjust to <i>her</i> ways as much as she can. She is also incredible strong and amazing with her sword and a fight would probably be almost an even match between the two. And he is still very much a sexy, powerful, leading man who allegedly hates it when she doesn't listen because everyone else does. And you still very much want them to be together because they are true equals.<br /><br />I know it really isn't the same genre, it's not a romance series so the romance is spread throughout several books before culmination but the idea is that women don't have to be whipped into submission to be with a powerful man. <br /><br />So that's a long review for a book I haven't read but I've felt the need to vent this for a long time and this was a good place to do so. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7071224624420880819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2674960307?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="NMmomof4" class="user" itemprop="url" name="NMmomof4" href="/user/show/24665574-nmmomof4">NMmomof4</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2674960307" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4008281674020884433"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/><b>Overall Opinion: </b> It's no secret that I'm not completely sold on PNR romance. This, while enjoyable, unfortunately didn't sell me any more. It was a little bit better than alright. I felt like the sexy times were definitely hot, but the actual romantic chemistry was lacking. It felt like the shared "ILYs" were put in because it was something that felt necessary, but I never quite felt it. The world building felt a little too much, but I get that this is he first book in a series and it </span>
  <span id="freeText4008281674020884433" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br /><br /><b>Overall Opinion: </b> It's no secret that I'm not completely sold on PNR romance. This, while enjoyable, unfortunately didn't sell me any more. It was a little bit better than alright. I felt like the sexy times were definitely hot, but the actual romantic chemistry was lacking. It felt like the shared "ILYs" were put in because it was something that felt necessary, but I never quite felt it. The world building felt a little too much, but I get that this is he first book in a series and it probably was necessary for the rest of the books...this is one issue I seem to have with the PNR genre in general. Otherwise, I really enjoyed the Valkyries and their brand of crazy and it was enjoyable at times.<br /><br /><b>Brief Summary of the Storyline: </b> This is Emma and Lachlain's story. Lachlain, the Lykae (werewolf) king, has spent nearly a decade under the torture of the vampire king when he finally scents his mate and escapes to find her. Emma, a half-vampire-half-Valkyrie, is on the search for information about her heritage when she is found and held captive by Lachlain. Lachlain is surprised by who is mate is, but he knows it's true and must get back to his home to have her become his queen and start out his vengeance against the vampires. There are some hot sexy times, some big secrets revealed, and some funny family moments...and they get a HFN ending.<br /><br /><b>Point Of View (POV):</b> This alternated between Emma and Lachlain's POV.<br /><br /><b>Overall Pace of Story: </b> Slow at first, but then it picks up to a good pace.<br /><br /><b>Instalove:</b> No, they take a while to develop stronger feelings (other than lust)<br /><br /><b>H (Hero) rating:</b> 4 stars. Lachlain. I liked him, but I did feel like we needed to get into his psyche a little more, especially because he was so old.<br /><br /><b>h (heroine) rating:</b> 4 stars. Emma. I liked her. She was sassy, strong (even when she viewed herself otherwise), and loyal.<br /><br /><b>Sadness level: </b>Low, no tissues needed<br /><br /><b>Push/Pull:</b> Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The h pushes away a good bit, and I'd say the H is the main pursuer of e relationship.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Heat level:</b> Hot. They have some hot tension, chemistry, and scenes -- but not so much it takes away from the story.<br /><br /><b>Descriptive sex:</b> Yes<br /><br /><b>OW (Other Woman)/OM (Other Man) drama:</b> Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ There is another woman that used to be with the H before he met the h that is around and causes some drama. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Sex scene with OW or OM:</b> No<br /><br /><b>Cheating: </b> No<br /><br /><b>Separation:</b> Yes, but not in the relationship sense <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[They are separated physically shortly, but there was no mention or suggestion of other partners during this time.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Possible Triggers: </b>Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Abuse/torture (through memories on page), violence/murder (on page), captivity (on page), borderline sexual assault (H to h on page), and the h was a virgin. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Closure: </b> This ends so abruptly that I was confused tbh. I read it with my Scribd subscription and it ended on page 377 of 526. I still had unanswered questions and I feel like it's probably one of those that will revisit this couple in the books later in the series. But! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[They're together, shared "ILYs" and Emma’s family has accepted the union <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> So I'd probably call it a HFN ending because of everything else that wasn't addressed but I felt needed to be.<br /><br /><b>Safety:</b> This one should be <u>Safe</u> for most safety gang readers<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have cheating<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have a descriptive sex scene with OW/OM<br />- <b> Does</b> have the h pushing the H away<br />- <b> Does</b> have a separation between the h and H<br />- <b> Does </b> have abuse<br />- <b>Does Not </b> have a HEA ending <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11833915731326037401"><blockquote>
  <b>⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱*Might contain spoilers*⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱</b>

  <u>Re-read: 15.05.17</u>
</b><br/>Why I found myself re-reading this one, I have no idea. But I sat at the airport and I just wanted to give it another shot, to see if I like it better this time around... <b>Lachlain MacRieve</b> (1200?) and <b>Emmaline Troy</b> (71?) are mates. Not as in Australian mate for 'buddy', but mates as in fated ones. However, having just escaped from the torture from the vampire horde (150 years?), Lachlain isn't all that happy with having a vampire mate.</span>
  <span id="freeText11833915731326037401" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱*Might contain spoilers*⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱</b>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>Re-read: 15.05.17</u>
</b><br>Why I found myself re-reading this one, I have no idea. But I sat at the airport and I just wanted to give it another shot, to see if I like it better this time around... <b>Lachlain MacRieve</b> (1200?) and <b>Emmaline Troy</b> (71?) are mates. Not as in Australian mate for 'buddy', but mates as in fated ones. However, having just escaped from the torture from the vampire horde (150 years?), Lachlain isn't all that happy with having a vampire mate. Although, Lachlain soon realized that there is more to the innocent, sweet yet feisty Emma...<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>When he watched her sleeping, he often thought, My heart lies vulnerable outside my chest.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>There's a somewhat insta-love here</b>, as well as fated/true mates. It takes what? Two weeks or so for the '<i>I have fallen in love</i>' words? Though the story is interesting, the constant back and forth: the characters take one step forward, two steps back, is really frustrating and makes things hard to really enjoy that book. <b>Overall, it's a alright read</b>, specially if you like a female character finding herself, becoming the woman she's meant to be and a man realizing revenge isn't everything, but not the best paranormal romance out there. I think I'm gonna re-read <b>
  <i>Lothaire</i>
</b> as well. To see if I'll have any better luck with that one. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Never run from one such as me, female. You will no’ get away - and we like it.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b><u>Quick basic facts</u>:</b><br><b>Genre</b>: - (Adult) Paranormal Romance<br><b>Series</b>: - Series (Standalone?), Book Two<br><b>Love triangle?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>Cheating?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>HEA?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yes. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>Favorite character?</b> - Lachlain MacRieve.<br><b>Would I read more by this author/or of series?</b> - Yes.<br><b>Would I recommend this book/series?</b> - I thin so?<br><b>Will I read this again in the future?</b> - No.<br><b>Rating</b> - 2.5/3 stars.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445268775i/16623124.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b><u>First read review</u>:</b><br>I liked it, but I didn't...get it?<br><b>Rate: 2.5/3 stars.</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_30940884" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/30940884" />
    <a title="Cris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1449734-cris"><img alt="Cris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1219448192p2/1449734.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/30940884?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cris" href="/user/show/1449734-cris">Cris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1449734-cris?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1449734-cris?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer30940884" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8115237008163498026">Basically I despised Lachlain MacRieve. He is an alpha character with no redeeming qualities. He treats Emma like crap for the first half of the novel. He takes her hostage, blackmails her into staying with him by threatening her family’s safety with his clan, lies to her about why he’s kidnapping her, comes within inches of raping her and that’s all within the first 100 pages or so. The author implies at some point that his treatment of her is justified because Lachlain hates vampires, but I ne</span>
  <span id="freeText8115237008163498026" style="display:none">Basically I despised Lachlain MacRieve. He is an alpha character with no redeeming qualities. He treats Emma like crap for the first half of the novel. He takes her hostage, blackmails her into staying with him by threatening her family’s safety with his clan, lies to her about why he’s kidnapping her, comes within inches of raping her and that’s all within the first 100 pages or so. The author implies at some point that his treatment of her is justified because Lachlain hates vampires, but I never got the feeling he was reacting to Emma as a vampire. (Not least of which because even he keeps forgetting she’s a vampire because she doesn’t act *anything* like a vampire.) And hatred for someone’s race isn’t a good enough reason for behaving badly anyway.<br /><br />Basically for the first half of the book Lachlain acts like Emma’s his sex toy or possession (*his* mate to do with as *he* wishes) rather a person who might have thoughts or feelings of her own. The second half of the book, after one of Emma’s aunts threatens him, he suddenly starts acting a little better. (More of just your typical macho-alpha jerk behavior. But his behavioral change didn’t seem to be accompanied by any deep or meaningful character change and he didn’t really express remorse for his behavior.)<br /><br /><b>Characterization: </b>Stinks. Emma’s aunts are rather funny and zany, but very one-dimensional. The other Lykae are very stereotypical types, and so are the bad guys. Emma’s the only half-way original character and we don’t get nearly enough insight into her.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8115237008163498026" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa Kay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa Kay" href="/user/show/2459470-lisa-kay">Lisa Kay</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=authors-c">authors-c</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=genre-romance-vampire">genre-romance-vampire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=re-read-for-comfort">re-read-for-comfort</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2459470-lisa-kay?shelf=authors-k">authors-k</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer61116092" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9028144679906167054">I have to confess that Emmaline Troy is one of my favorite heroines in a paranormal romance. Sometimes-only sometimes -I get especially tired of books where the heroine is the feisty, aggressive person right from the get-go. Did they pop from the womb, full Rambo-ette, ready to take on the world? (My friend swears her daughter did.) How did they get that way? It is sometimes more interesting to see a meek personality like Emma develop. Yes, she has been sheltered and she's a wuss, but she grows </span>
  <span id="freeText9028144679906167054" style="display:none">I have to confess that Emmaline Troy is one of my favorite heroines in a paranormal romance. Sometimes-only sometimes -I get especially tired of books where the heroine is the feisty, aggressive person right from the get-go. Did they pop from the womb, full Rambo-ette, ready to take on the world? (My friend swears her daughter did.) How did they get that way? It is sometimes more interesting to see a meek personality like Emma develop. Yes, she has been sheltered and she's a wuss, but she grows into a beautiful, complex blend of Vampire and Valkyrie. Plus, I loved her wardrobe. She doesn’t have a dog like most of my favorite heroines do…but wait, I forgot, Lachlain MacRieve fits that bill. :)<br /><br />I also have to confess that, up until Emma, I didn't read a lot of paranormal romances. I had read all of Kresley Cole's books. That is another reason this is on my 'all-time-favorites' bookshelf. It was the one that opened me up to the genre.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9028144679906167054" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_89319150" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Zeek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2478293-zeek"><img alt="Zeek" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339154824p2/2478293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/89319150?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zeek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zeek" href="/user/show/2478293-zeek">Zeek</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2478293-zeek?shelf=favorites-pnr">favorites-pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2478293-zeek?shelf=uber-alpha-male">uber-alpha-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2478293-zeek?shelf=favorites-all-time">favorites-all-time</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2478293-zeek?shelf=favorite-author">favorite-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2478293-zeek?shelf=pnr-kitchen-sink">pnr-kitchen-sink</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2478293-zeek?shelf=alpha-hero">alpha-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2478293-zeek?shelf=favorite-hero">favorite-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2478293-zeek?shelf=shifters">shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2478293-zeek?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer89319150" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10437557263056463816">First full length novel in Cole's paranormal romance series Immortals After Dark, (second overall), A Hunger Like No Other is a gold mine of uber-alpha, destined-for-each other, sexy reading.<br/><br/>When Lachlain scents his mate while hidden below the streets of Paris, he does the impossible- he breaks the chains that have kept him imprisoned for 150 years and goes after her. Sure he tears off a limb to do so, but he's a werewolf- so regeneration, though painful, is possible.<br/><br/>Emmaline has lived as an acc</span>
  <span id="freeText10437557263056463816" style="display:none">First full length novel in Cole's paranormal romance series Immortals After Dark, (second overall), A Hunger Like No Other is a gold mine of uber-alpha, destined-for-each other, sexy reading.<br /><br />When Lachlain scents his mate while hidden below the streets of Paris, he does the impossible- he breaks the chains that have kept him imprisoned for 150 years and goes after her. Sure he tears off a limb to do so, but he's a werewolf- so regeneration, though painful, is possible.<br /><br />Emmaline has lived as an accepted outsider with her Valkyrie Aunts all her life. Half Vampire, half Valkyrie, Emma is the non-confrontational one of the bunch ... but that's about to change.<br /><br />Storming into her life with the force of a hurricane, Lachlain is disgusted when he discovers the woman he's waited for, for almost a thousand years, is a vampire- the hated enemy of his clan. None-the-less he takes her hostage, deciding he'll keep her because there's no way he's losing his mate now that he's found her.<br /><br />Weakened by not feeding for days, Emma is lethargic and scared out of her mind by the overbearing were who's hijacked her and talked her into joining him on his return trip home to Scotland. But when she takes his blood for the first time, her strength returns full force and the creature known as Emma the Timid takes a drastic turn.<br /><br />Even as Lachlain's "beast" is soothed by finally being with his mate, Emma finds she is not so timid after all and so she does whatever she can to get away from the impossible man who claims he wants her above all others.<br /><br />In the meantime, she's having strange dreams from Lachlain's point of view and as they spend time together, finds herself just as drawn to him as he is to her.<br /><br />So much so, when she does find her chance to escape- instead of running home- she heads straight for the deadly vampire who ruined Lachlain's life.<br /><br />Sacrificing her own desires, she finds the courage to kill a king ... and in process accept her fate as a creature of Three.<br /><br />Archetypal Paranormal Romance, AHLNO is a thrilling ride I couldn't get off of till the very last word!<br /><br />Here's the thing though, Cole's writes some over the top alpha heroes. Not usually a problem for me because I find non-alpha heroes in romantic fiction never hold my interest very long. However, she writes them SO alpha, I often cringe at their antics, which tend to come off as bullying.<br /><br />Just as when I read If You Dare, 1st in a historical romance series by this author, I wasn't sure if I would ever like the hero ... until about a quarter of the way through when he began to change. And too, the heroine irritated the heck out of me for being so unrelentingly angry at the hero through much of the rest of book!<br /><br />Yet through it all, I closed the book thinking, "that was a good read."<br /><br />I suppose the setting, the fantasy-like creatures, and yes, the strong romantic elements is enough to make it a winner in the long run. Either way, I'm certainly rushing out to get the rest in the series! :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="10437557263056463816" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_76995512" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/76995512" />
    <a title="Kiki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2828633-kiki"><img alt="Kiki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339004346p2/2828633.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/76995512?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kiki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kiki" href="/user/show/2828633-kiki">Kiki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">women who want to meet their perfect man when he gives them Stockholm Syndrome</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer76995512&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer76995512" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2550305852360541864">I hate this book more than I've hated any other book in a long time.<br/><br/>At first I really liked the idea of a vampire character who is so gentle she refuses to fight or kill or drink from a live being. But then it turns out that not only is her Valkyrie family embarrassed she's a pacifist, they mercilessly make fun of her for it. But wait, they also tell her that she's not allowed to bite a human, because she might kill them. So, it's OK to kill in epic battle, but not for food? Apparently, Emmeline</span>
  <span id="freeText2550305852360541864" style="display:none">I hate this book more than I've hated any other book in a long time.<br /><br />At first I really liked the idea of a vampire character who is so gentle she refuses to fight or kill or drink from a live being. But then it turns out that not only is her Valkyrie family embarrassed she's a pacifist, they mercilessly make fun of her for it. But wait, they also tell her that she's not allowed to bite a human, because she might kill them. So, it's OK to kill in epic battle, but not for food? Apparently, Emmeline eventually get her I-am-Vampire/Valkyrie-hear-me-have-a-15-page-fight-scene on, but I wouldn't know, since I only read the first 40-or-so pages.<br /><br />But here's the real reason I only read that far: I'm not really into romances that stem from attempted rape. In one of the more chilling encounters I've read, our heroine meets her "mate" when he's one a destructive rampage through Paris, looking for her. He finds her, rips her blouse and bra open to ogle her on a public street, and forcibly makes her take him back to her hotel. Once there, he kisses her, uttering such charming phrases as, "Kiss me back, witch, while I decide if I should spare your life," and "Kiss me like your life depends upon it." Then he makes her take a shower with him, during the duration of which he manhandles her, forces her to spread her legs and is about to rape her, which she only manages to circumnavigate by giving him a hand-job. <br /><br />And then he steals her credit card to buy himself a new wardrobe. (Note: if you look really menacing, concierges at fancy Parisian hotels will let you use an AmEx Black card with a woman's name on it, even if you are a man who has been trapped at the gates of hell for a thousand years.) <br /><br />And then he performs oral sex on her while she sleeps.<br /><br />Did I mention that she's a 70-year-old virgin who's never even had a kiss?<br /><br />But I guess the almighty mating bond (a trope I am so very tired of seeing) really does conquer all. Except my gag reflex.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_578909308" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/578909308" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4255477-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398251387p2/4255477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/578909308?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/4255477-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6473141-a-hunger-like-no-other">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2019-read">2019-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2014-read">2014-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer578909308" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5602431591588293096">May 2019 Re-read<br/><br/>7 April 2015: <a href='http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B000GCFCXW/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&camp=1789&creative=390957&creativeASIN=B000GCFCXW&linkCode=as2&tag=touthenig-20&linkId=7IJQECOITGPA47IA' rel='nofollow noopener'>$1.99 on Kindle</a><br/><br/>Review of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122560174' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Warlord Wants Forever</a><br/><br/>This is probably only my second or third read of this book, I'm buddy re-reading the series with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/102417898' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sarah</a> in preparation for the release of the <b>fourteenth</b> book in the series - someone's book that I've been looking forward to for a few years now. But I won't spoil that here.<br/><br/>Kresley Cole is a master of weaving together and intricate tale that involves overlapping storylines, and many, many characters. The <b>Immortals After </b></span>
  <span id="freeText5602431591588293096" style="display:none">May 2019 Re-read<br /><br />7 April 2015: <a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B000GCFCXW/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=390957&amp;creativeASIN=B000GCFCXW&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=touthenig-20&amp;linkId=7IJQECOITGPA47IA" rel="nofollow noopener">$1.99 on Kindle</a><br /><br />Review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122560174" rel="nofollow noopener">The Warlord Wants Forever</a><br /><br />This is probably only my second or third read of this book, I'm buddy re-reading the series with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/102417898" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah</a> in preparation for the release of the <b>fourteenth</b> book in the series - someone's book that I've been looking forward to for a few years now. But I won't spoil that here.<br /><br />Kresley Cole is a master of weaving together and intricate tale that involves overlapping storylines, and many, many characters. The <b>Immortals After Dark</b> world is populated by the Lore - immortal beings that have managed to hide themselves from humans, for the most part. There are Lykae - not the standard werewolves you may be thinking of; Witches, Vampires, Demons, Ghouls, Phantoms...and my personal favorite: Valkyries. All these factions fight for themselves, looking for their other half - whatever they call it, Mate, Bride, etc - and living their lives. Every five-hundred years comes the Accession to mess that up. As told in the book, the Accession...<br /><br /><blockquote><br />...Bringing prosperity and power to the victors, the Accession wasn't an Armageddon type of war--it wasn't as if the strongest factions of the Lore met on neutral turf after an invitation to "rumble." About a decade into it, events began to come into play, as if fate was seeding future, deadly conflicts, involving all the players at a startling rate. Like windmill vanes on a rusted spoke, it began creaking, creeping to life, only to gain momentum and soar with speed every five hundred years.<br /><br />Some said it was a kind of cosmic checks-and-balances system for an ever-growing population of immortals, forcing them to kill each other off.<br /><br />In the end, the faction that lost the fewest of their kind won.</blockquote><br /><br />So here we are; at the beginning of what many in the Lore are starting to believe is the start of the Accession. A time when immortals find their mates - sometimes in very unexpected places, alliances are made or discord is sown between the different factions of the Lore.<br /><br />I'm speaking a lot about the world, because after thirteen books it's still my favorite thing about this series. The world and overall plotting is <i>masterful</i>. Kresley Cole blows my mind time and time again with the way she casually ties things together, references events we won't hear about for books to come, and never once have I caught a slip or mistake in these books. I'm awed by the ability she has to keep it all straight. There's a side reference in this book, Book 2, that doesn't get fully explained until Book 9! All of these events are taking place so close together as to be on top of one another. You're always right in the middle of it, hoping that these characters you come to love will make it through.<br /><br />The other thing I can guarantee you, in every book, is that Kresley Cole <b>loves</b> to put her heroes and heroines through the wringer before giving them their HEA. Not just at the hands of others either - she pushes these characters to the very limits of what they might be able to forgive their fated other-half...and for some it might step over the line. I struggle with this from time to time. I read these books, I love these books, and even still I wonder if I shouldn't be objecting more to some of the treatment the characters do to one another. <br /><br />I suppose I should talk about the main characters of this book: Emma and Lachlain. Emma is the half-breed daughter of a vampire and a valkyrie. She's been raised by the valkyrie, hidden from the vampires, her entire life. Lachlain is the lykae king - imprisoned for 150 years (by vampires), he finally breaks free to find his mate.<br /><br />As you can imagine the fact that Emma is (part) vampire is a source of tremendous torture to Lachlain's fragile sanity. He can't imagine why he's been mated to one of his hated enemies, but still he fights to protect her, even from his own rages. I definitely understood what Lachlain was struggling with, and honestly his recovery is really, really quick - just the hell that he puts Emma through in the meantime can sometimes be cringe-worthy. I like him a lot. He's like the prototype of 'bash-em-over-the-head-and-drag-her-back-to-the-cave' type. But he's also all - and I do mean ALL - about making sure his mate is happy. He makes mistakes, so it's a good thing he's got Emma to call him on it, and bring him into line.<br /><br />Almost as much as I hate to say this, everything that happens to Emma just makes her stronger, more sure of herself, and more able to handle everything thrown at her. She starts the book as Emma the Timid. The most exciting thing she's ever done is go to Paris by herself to search for the father - whose name she doesn't even know. And even then she was protected by the money she had from the coven to protect her. She continues to think of herself as this in some small moments for about half the book. The truth is something far more complicated. Emma's been conditioned to think she's not good enough, not strong enough, not brave enough. It wasn't intentional, it wasn't anyone's fault, but the consequences of growing up with those that she did - the strong, brave, and fighting valkyries. She shows from very early on that she's not afraid to defend herself, think for herself, and stands up against Lachlain over and over again. <br /><br />I admit the first time I read this I didn't love Lachlain or Emma. I liked them both, but I was irritated with how Lachlain treated Emma (especially in the beginning), and Emma's timidity. I'd bought too much into her own image of herself instead of seeing what was <i>shown</i> to me. I loved Emma on this re-read. She's fantastic. She continues to grow and evolve as a character throughout the book, and kicks ass along the way. Lachlain I still have some problems with. He does some pretty neanderthal things, especially in the beginning, but I understand too. He's coming out of <b>fifteen decades</b> of torture, and has finally found his mate and is terrified that she might leave him. By the time Emma reached the end of the story I felt that Lachlain was a good match for her, and that they'd be great together.<br /><br />In the end, I ended up loving this book so much more than the first time I'd read it. the main characters are great, the world is phenomenal, the plot is amazing, and the secondary characters continue to make me wish for many, many more stories in this series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5602431591588293096" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_265405810" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/265405810" />
    <a title="Alex is The Romance Fox" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6663962-alex-is-the-romance-fox"><img alt="Alex is The Romance Fox" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1428866380p2/6663962.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/265405810?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex is The Romance Fox" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex is The Romance Fox" href="/user/show/6663962-alex-is-the-romance-fox">Alex is The Romance Fox</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781849834186" href="/book/show/9674479-a-hunger-like-no-other">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6663962-alex-is-the-romance-fox?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6663962-alex-is-the-romance-fox?shelf=vampire-shapeshifters">vampire-shapeshifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6663962-alex-is-the-romance-fox?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer265405810" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12073405406748071523">Talk about a rollercoaster ride!!!! This is the first book I have read by Kresley Cole and I liked, well loved A Hunger Like No Other.!!!! I like her writing style a lot – fresh, easy to read, words just flowing from page to page. Love scenes are hot, hot!!!! This is the story of Lachlain, the Lykean King, who finally finds his true life mate - Emmaline, a half-vampire/valkyrie.<br/>The Prologue is absolutely amazing…..heart-stopping suspense. Lachlain escaping from the Paris catacombs where he has b</span>
  <span id="freeText12073405406748071523" style="display:none">Talk about a rollercoaster ride!!!! This is the first book I have read by Kresley Cole and I liked, well loved A Hunger Like No Other.!!!! I like her writing style a lot – fresh, easy to read, words just flowing from page to page. Love scenes are hot, hot!!!! This is the story of Lachlain, the Lykean King, who finally finds his true life mate - Emmaline, a half-vampire/valkyrie.<br />The Prologue is absolutely amazing…..heart-stopping suspense. Lachlain escaping from the Paris catacombs where he has been held prisoner for hundreds of years by an evil Vampire makes you want to continue reading until you get to the last page….where you sigh wishing there were more pages..<br />Emmaline is the coolest vampire/valkyrie ever….love her style and look…..a sexy, sassy, hip and beyond gorgeous…..she’s my favorite female vampire right now!!!!! Sorry Bella!!!!!!!. How can Lachlain ever think he will be able to overcome his desire for her!!!!! No chance. He’s hooked!!! <br />Great plot filled with many twists and turns, loads of incredible characters (believe me there are a lot of them in this book )whose interaction between each other is really quite amazing ….the sexual built-up between the H/H is scorching hot…..you think…finally they are going to do it!!...and POW!!!!…no not this time!!!!!<br /> A world filled with vampires, demons, valkyries, witches, demons, ghouls, and many others. There’s romance, action, suspense and wit that you can’t wait to turn the next page to find out what happens next. <br />Some of the dialogue had me shrieking with laughter…..check it out…... <br />Emma – “How old?”<br />Lachlain – Roughly twelve hundred years.”<br />She gasped. “Do you know what “robbing the cradle” means? I am almost seventy one. This skeeves me out!”<br /><br />"Hey, Lucia," Regin called out, not even bothering to mute the phone. "Pay up, suckah, Emma got dental with some dude—"<br /><br />"You can have him, kitties," she hissed for their ears only.<br /><br />Christ, he couldn't do this. "How do you drink?"<br />She mumbled, "Liquid goes into my mouth, whereby I swallow it."<br /><br />Is your blouse Azzedine Alaia?" the girl showing them to their table asked Emma.<br />She answered, "No, you could say it's very authentic vintage."<br /><br />"Lachlain, have you ever heard of a Wal-Mart? No? Something like that is probably on top of your castle right now."<br /><br />Was she becoming this Lykae's Patty Hearst?<br /><br />"I am Lachlain. Who are you?"<br />"I'm the foster mother who's going to annihilate you if you don't send her home right now.<br /><br />Bowe raised his eyebrows, demonstrating the most emotion Lachlain had seen from him since his mate had left him. "A vampire queen? Fate must hate you." More examination while Lachlain scowled. "Her ears are pointed?"<br /><br />If you want a funny, sexy, steamy, hot paranormal romance, then go and get the book right now!!!! I promise you will enjoy the ride!!!!!<br />I finished reading this book in two days….and immediately tried to get the next in the series……unlucky me ….haven’t managed to find a copy…but will keep on trying…..cause I am now a KC fan and want to read the whole series.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12073405406748071523" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xT8gHIApCnqAzD9k2CE2aaNo+0e58EOKYZ03IHEGoQRxvtIayJM61QlVGJC8bIA6CWcAfPffCZKWhtUL/zM3iQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AMZ7ggQ61BovOcoLmEaz0aWpr2MdBWqD0NTLJ96F0aS0R4mETIDktaag7f/8CwWCD6ZUWFMqIJsnzykMULBHKQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer17702047242080995373">Kresley Cole is the #1 <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of the electrifying Immortals After Dark paranormal series, the young adult Arcana Chronicles series, the erotic Gamemakers series, and five award-winning historical romances.<br/><br/>A master’s grad and former athlete, she has traveled over much of the world and draws from those experiences to create her memorable characters and settings. <br/>Her IAD bo</span>
  <span id="freeText17702047242080995373" style="display:none">Kresley Cole is the #1 <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of the electrifying Immortals After Dark paranormal series, the young adult Arcana Chronicles series, the erotic Gamemakers series, and five award-winning historical romances.<br /><br />A master’s grad and former athlete, she has traveled over much of the world and draws from those experiences to create her memorable characters and settings. <br />Her IAD books have been translated into 23 foreign languages, garnered three RITA awards, a RWA Hall of Fame induction, and consistently appear on the bestseller lists, in the U.S. and abroad.<br /><br />Cole lives in Florida with her family. Learn more about Kresley at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.kresleycole.com">www.kresleycole.com</a> &amp; <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.thearcanachronicles.com">www.thearcanachronicles.com</a><br /><br /></span>
